</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg/220px-Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg/330px-Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg/440px-Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations_1320588_nevit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations" title="Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</a> (1921)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara" title="Ethnography Museum of Ankara">Ankara Ethnography Museum</a> (<i>Etnoğrafya Müzesi</i>) is located opposite to the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House" title="Ankara Opera House">Ankara Opera House</a> on Talat Paşa Boulevard, in the Ulus district. There is a fine collection of folkloric items, as well as artifacts from the Seljuk and Ottoman periods. In front of the museum building, there is a <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue" title="Equestrian statue">equestrian statue</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a> (who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" title="Field Marshal" class="mw-redirect">Field Marshal</a>) which was crafted in 1927 by the renowned Italian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Canonica" title="Pietro Canonica">Pietro Canonica</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations" title="Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</a> (<i>Anadolu Medeniyetleri Müzesi</i>) is situated at the entrance of the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Castle" title="Ankara Castle">Ankara Castle</a>. It is an old <a href="/wiki/Bedesten" title="Bedesten">bedesten</a> (covered bazaar) that has been beautifully restored and now houses a unique collection of <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hittite_empire" title="Hittite empire" class="mw-redirect">Hatti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">Phrygian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">Urartian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> works as well as a major section dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydian</a> treasures.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="State_Art_and_Sculpture_Museum">State Art and Sculpture Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: State Art and Sculpture Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/State_Art_and_Sculpture_Museum" title="State Art and Sculpture Museum">State Art and Sculpture Museum</a> (<i>Resim-Heykel Müzesi</i>) is close to the Ethnography Museum and houses a rich collection of Turkish art from the late 19th century to the present day. There are also galleries which host guest exhibitions.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cer_Modern">Cer Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cer Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cermodern.org/">Cer Modern</a> is the modern-arts museum of Ankara, inaugurated on 1 April 2010. It is situated in the renovated building of the historic <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways" title="Turkish State Railways">TCDD</a> Cer Atölyeleri, formerly a workshop of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways" title="Turkish State Railways">Turkish State Railways</a>. The museum incorporates the largest exhibition hall in Turkey. The museum holds periodic exhibitions of modern and contemporary art as well as hosting other contemporary arts events.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_Independence_Museum">War of Independence Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: War of Independence Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_Museum" title="War of Independence Museum">War of Independence Museum</a> (<i>Kurtuluş Savaşı Müzesi</i>) is located on <a href="/wiki/Ulus_Square" title="Ulus Square">Ulus Square</a>. It was originally the first Parliament building (TBMM) of the Republic of Turkey. The War of Independence was planned and directed here as recorded in various photographs and items presently on exhibition. In another display, <a href="/wiki/Wax_sculpture" title="Wax sculpture">wax figures</a> of former presidents of the Republic of Turkey are on exhibit.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mehmet_Akif_Literature_Museum_Library">Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg/220px-ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg/330px-ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg/440px-ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3664" data-file-height="2748" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ODT%C3%9C_Bilim_ve_Teknoloji_M%C3%BCzesi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/METU_Science_and_Technology_Museum" title="METU Science and Technology Museum">METU Science and Technology Museum</a> in Ankara.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Akif_Literature_Museum_Library" title="Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library" class="mw-redirect">Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library</a> is a literary museum and archive opened in 2011 and dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Akif_Ersoy" title="Mehmet Akif Ersoy">Mehmet Akif Ersoy</a> (1873–1936), the poet of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_National_Anthem" title="Turkish National Anthem" class="mw-redirect">Turkish National Anthem</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="TCDD_Open_Air_Steam_Locomotive_Museum">TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/TCDD_Open_Air_Steam_Locomotive_Museum" title="TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum">TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Open-air_museum" title="Open-air museum">open-air museum</a> which traces the history of <a href="/wiki/Steam_locomotive" title="Steam locomotive">steam locomotives</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ankara_Aviation_Museum">Ankara Aviation Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ankara Aviation Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ankara Aviation Museum (<i>Hava Kuvvetleri Müzesi Komutanlığı</i>) is located near the Istanbul Road in Etimesgut. It is home to various missiles, avionics, aviation materials and aircraft that have served in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Air_Force" title="Turkish Air Force">Turkish Air Force</a> (e.g. combat aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/F-86_Sabre" title="F-86 Sabre" class="mw-redirect">F-86 Sabre</a>, <a href="/wiki/F-100_Super_Sabre" title="F-100 Super Sabre" class="mw-redirect">F-100 Super Sabre</a>, <a href="/wiki/F-102_Delta_Dagger" title="F-102 Delta Dagger" class="mw-redirect">F-102 Delta Dagger</a>, <a href="/wiki/F-104_Starfighter" title="F-104 Starfighter" class="mw-redirect">F-104 Starfighter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5" title="Northrop F-5">F-5 Freedom Fighter</a>, <a href="/wiki/F-4_Phantom_II" title="F-4 Phantom II" class="mw-redirect">F-4 Phantom</a>; and cargo planes such as the <a href="/wiki/Transall_C-160" title="Transall C-160">Transall C-160</a>.) Also a Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-21">MiG-21</a>, a Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-19" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-19">MiG-19</a>, and a Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-17" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-17">MiG-17</a> are on display at the museum.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="METU_Science_and_Technology_Museum">METU Science and Technology Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: METU Science and Technology Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/METU_Science_and_Technology_Museum" title="METU Science and Technology Museum">METU Science and Technology Museum</a> (<i>ODTÜ Bilim ve Teknoloji Müzesi</i>) is located inside the <a href="/wiki/METU" title="METU" class="mw-redirect">Middle East Technical University</a> campus.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg/220px-Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg/330px-Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg/440px-Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1041" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_by_night_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ksu_Park" title="Göksu Park">Göksu Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dikmen_Vadisi,_Ankara_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg/220px-Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg/330px-Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg/440px-Dikmen_Vadisi%2C_Ankara_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dikmen_Vadisi,_Ankara_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dikmen Valley Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ankara has many parks and open spaces mainly established in the early years of the Republic and well maintained and expanded thereafter. The most important of these parks are: <a href="/wiki/Gen%C3%A7lik_Park%C4%B1" title="Gençlik Parkı">Gençlik Parkı</a> (houses an <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a> with a large pond for rowing), the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">Botanical garden</a>, Seğmenler Park, Anayasa Park, <a href="/wiki/Ku%C4%9Fulu_Park" title="Kuğulu Park">Kuğulu Park</a> (famous for the swans received as a gift from the <a href="/wiki/PRC" title="PRC" class="mw-redirect">Chinese</a> government), <a href="/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i" title="Abdi İpekçi">Abdi İpekçi</a> Park, <a href="/wiki/Esertepe_Park%C4%B1" title="Esertepe Parkı" class="mw-redirect">Esertepe Parkı</a>, Güven Park (see above for the monument), Kurtuluş Park (has an ice-skating rink), <a href="/wiki/Alt%C4%B1npark" title="Altınpark">Altınpark</a> (also a prominent exposition/fair area), Harikalar Diyarı (claimed to be Biggest Park of Europe inside city borders) and Göksu Park.</p>
<p>Gençlik Park was depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the Turkish 100 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknotes of 1952–1976.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Forest_Farm_and_Zoo" title="Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo">Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo</a> (<i>Atatürk Orman Çiftliği</i>) is an expansive recreational farming area which houses a <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoo</a>, several small agricultural farms, <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a>, restaurants, a <a href="/wiki/Dairy_farming" title="Dairy farming">dairy farm</a> and a brewery. It is a pleasant place to spend a day with family, be it for having picnics, hiking, biking or simply enjoying good food and nature. There is also an exact replica of the house where Atatürk was born in 1881, in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, Greece. Visitors to the "Çiftlik" (farm) as it is affectionately called by Ankarans, can sample such famous products of the farm such as old-fashioned beer and <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a>, fresh <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a> and meat rolls/kebaps made on charcoal, at a traditional restaurant (<i>Merkez Lokantası</i>, Central Restaurant), cafés and other establishments scattered around the farm.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Atakule.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ankara_Atakule.JPG/220px-Ankara_Atakule.JPG" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ankara_Atakule.JPG/330px-Ankara_Atakule.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ankara_Atakule.JPG/440px-Ankara_Atakule.JPG 2x" data-file-width="989" data-file-height="685" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Atakule.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Atakule_Tower" title="Atakule Tower" class="mw-redirect">Atakule Tower</a> (1989)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG/220px-A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG/330px-A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG/440px-A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Sheraton_Ankara_from_Karum_Shopping_Mall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sheraton_Ankara" title="Sheraton Ankara">Sheraton Ankara</a> rising behind <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Turkey#Ankara" title="List of shopping malls in Turkey">Karum shopping mall</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kavakl%C4%B1dere,_Ankara" title="Kavaklıdere, Ankara">Kavaklıdere</a> quarter of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara" title="Çankaya, Ankara">Çankaya</a> business and leisure district.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Foreign visitors to Ankara usually like to visit the old shops in <i>Çıkrıkçılar Yokuşu</i> (Weavers' Road) near Ulus, where myriad things ranging from traditional fabrics, hand-woven carpets and leather products can be found at bargain prices. <i>Bakırcılar Çarşısı</i> (Bazaar of Coppersmiths) is particularly popular, and many interesting items, not just of copper, can be found here like jewelry, carpets, costumes, antiques and embroidery. Up the hill to the castle gate, there are many shops selling a huge and fresh collection of spices, <a href="/wiki/Dried_fruit" title="Dried fruit">dried fruits</a>, nuts, and other produce.</p>
<p>Modern shopping areas are mostly found in <a href="/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay,_Ankara" title="Kızılay, Ankara">Kızılay</a>, or on Tunalı Hilmi Avenue, including the modern mall of <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Turkey#Ankara" title="List of shopping malls in Turkey">Karum</a> (named after the ancient <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> merchant colonies called <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BCltepe#K.C3.A2rum_Kane.C5.A1" title="Kültepe"><i>Kârum</i></a> that were established in <a href="/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region" title="Central Anatolia Region">central</a> <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2nd_millennium_BC" title="2nd millennium BC">2nd millennium BC</a>) which is located towards the end of the Avenue; and in <a href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara" title="Çankaya, Ankara">Çankaya</a>, the quarter with the highest elevation in the city. <a href="/wiki/Atakule" title="Atakule">Atakule Tower</a> next to <a href="/wiki/Atakule#Atrium_shopping_mall" title="Atakule">Atrium Mall</a> in Çankaya commands a magnificent view over Ankara and also has a <a href="/wiki/Revolving_restaurant" title="Revolving restaurant">revolving restaurant</a> at the top, where the city's panorama can be enjoyed in a leisurely fashion. The symbol of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Turkey#Ankara" title="List of shopping malls in Turkey">Armada Shopping Mall</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a>, and there's a large anchor monument at its entrance, as a reference to the ancient Greek name of the city, Ἄγκυρα (Ánkyra), which means anchor. Likewise, the anchor monument is also related with the Spanish name of the mall, Armada, which means <a href="/wiki/Naval_fleet" title="Naval fleet">naval fleet</a>.</p>
<p>As Ankara started expanding westward in the 1970s, several modern, suburbia-style developments and mini-cities began to rise along the western highway, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir" title="Eskişehir">Eskişehir</a> Road. The <i>Armada</i>,<i>CEPA</i> and <i>Kentpark</i> malls on the highway, the <i>Galleria</i>, <i>Arcadium</i> and <i>Gordion</i> in Ümitköy, and a huge mall, <i>Real</i> in Bilkent Center, offer North American and European style shopping opportunities (these places can be reached through the Eskişehir Highway.) There is also the newly expanded <i><a href="/wiki/ANKAmall" title="ANKAmall">ANKAmall</a></i> at the outskirts, on the Istanbul Highway, which houses most of the well-known international brands. This mall is the largest throughout the Ankara region. In 2014 a few more shopping malls were open in Ankara. They are <i>Next Level</i> and <i>Taurus</i> on the Boulevard of <a href="/wiki/Mevlana" title="Mevlana" class="mw-redirect">Mevlana</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Konya" title="Konya">Konya</a> Road).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archeological_sites">Archeological sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Archeological sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ankara_Citadel">Ankara Citadel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Ankara Citadel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG/220px-Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG/330px-Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG/440px-Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2034" data-file-height="1096" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Castle_walls.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ankara_Castle" title="Ankara Castle">Ankara citadel walls</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg/220px-MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg/330px-MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg/440px-MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="739" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MonumentumAncyranum28Nov2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In the <i>Temple of Augustus and Rome</i> (commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a>) in Ulus, the primary intact copy of <a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae</a> written by the first Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> survives.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The foundations of the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Castle" title="Ankara Castle">Ankara castle and citadel</a> were laid by the Galatians on a prominent <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lava</a> outcrop (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Ankara&amp;params=39.941_N_32.864_E_type:landmark"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">39°56′28″N</span> <span class="longitude">32°51′50″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">39.941°N 32.864°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">39.941; 32.864</span></span></span></a></span>), and the rest was completed by the Romans. The Byzantines and Seljuks further made restorations and additions. The area around and inside the citadel, being the oldest part of Ankara, contains many fine examples of traditional architecture. There are also recreational areas to relax. Many restored traditional Turkish houses inside the citadel area have found new life as restaurants, serving local cuisine.</p>
<p>The citadel was depicted in various Turkish banknotes during 1927–1952 and 1983–1989.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Theatre">Roman Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Roman Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The remains, the stage, and the backstage of the Roman theatre can be seen outside <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Castle" title="Ankara Castle">the castle</a>. Roman statues that were found here are exhibited in the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations" title="Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</a>. The seating area is still under excavation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temple_of_Augustus_and_Rome">Temple of Augustus and Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Temple of Augustus and Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a></div>
<p>The Augusteum,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1911b_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1911b-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> now known as the Temple of Augustus and Rome, was built 25&#160;<abbr title="sometime between">x</abbr>&#160;20&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="FONT-VARIANT: SMALL-CAPS; TEXT-TRANSFORM: LOWERCASE;">BC</span></span> following the conquest of Central Anatolia by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. Ancyra then formed the capital of the new <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Galatia" title="Galatia">Galatia</a>. After the death of <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="FONT-VARIANT: SMALL-CAPS; TEXT-TRANSFORM: LOWERCASE;">AD</span></span>&#160;14, a copy of the text of the <i><a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae Divi Augusti</a></i> (the <i><a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a></i>) was inscribed on the interior of the temple's <i><span lang="la">pronaos</span></i> in Latin and a Greek translation on an exterior wall of the <i><span lang="la">cella</span></i>. The temple on the ancient acropolis of Ancyra was enlarged in the 2nd century and converted into a church by the in the 5th century, . It is located in the Ulus quarter of the city. It was subsequently publicized by the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> ambassador <a href="/wiki/Ogier_Ghiselin_de_Busbecq" title="Ogier Ghiselin de Busbecq">Ogier Ghiselin de Busbecq</a> in the 16th century.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Baths">Roman Baths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Roman Baths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Baths_of_Ankara" title="Roman Baths of Ankara">Roman Baths of Ankara</a> have all the typical features of a classical <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">Roman bath complex</a>: a <i><a href="/wiki/Frigidarium" title="Frigidarium">frigidarium</a></i> (cold room), a <i><a href="/wiki/Tepidarium" title="Tepidarium">tepidarium</a></i> (warm room) and a <i><a href="/wiki/Caldarium" title="Caldarium">caldarium</a></i> (hot room). The baths were built during the reign of the Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Caracalla" title="Caracalla">Caracalla</a> in the early 3rd century to honor <a href="/wiki/Asclepius" title="Asclepius">Asclepios</a>, the God of Medicine. Today, only the basement and first floors remain. It is situated in the Ulus quarter.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Road">Roman Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Roman Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Road_of_Ankara" title="Roman Road of Ankara">Roman Road of Ankara</a> or <i>Cardo Maximus</i> was found in 1995 by Turkish archaeologist Cevdet Bayburtluoğlu. It is 216 meters long and 6.7 meters wide. Many ancient artifacts were discovered during the excavations along the road and most of them are currently displayed at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations" title="Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Antik_Ankara_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antik_Ankara-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Column_of_Julian">Column of Julian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Column of Julian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Column of Julian or Julianus, now in the Ulus district, was erected in honor of the Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate" class="mw-redirect">Julian the Apostate</a>'s visit to Ancyra in 362.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mosques">Mosques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mosques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg/220px-Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg/330px-Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg/440px-Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4569" data-file-height="3137" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hacı Bayram Mosque</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KocatepeMosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/KocatepeMosque.jpg/170px-KocatepeMosque.jpg" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/KocatepeMosque.jpg/255px-KocatepeMosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/KocatepeMosque.jpg/340px-KocatepeMosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2501" data-file-height="3534" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KocatepeMosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kocatepe_Mosque" title="Kocatepe Mosque">Kocatepe Mosque</a> (1989) is the largest mosque in Ankara.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Alaeddin_Mosque">Alaeddin Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Alaeddin Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Alaeddin Mosque is the oldest mosque in Ankara. It has a <a href="/wiki/Wood_carving" title="Wood carving">carved</a> <a href="/wiki/Juglans" title="Juglans">walnut</a> <a href="/wiki/Minbar" title="Minbar">mimber</a>, the inscription on which records that the mosque was completed in early <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calendar" title="Islamic calendar">AH 574</a> (which corresponds to the summer of 1178 AD) and was built by the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty" title="Seljuk dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Seljuk</a> prince Muhiddin Mesud Şah (d. 1204), the <a href="/wiki/Bey" title="Bey">Bey</a> of Ankara, who was the son of the <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_Seljuk_Sultanate" title="Anatolian Seljuk Sultanate" class="mw-redirect">Anatolian Seljuk sultan</a> <a href="/wiki/Kilij_Arslan_II" title="Kilij Arslan II">Kılıç Arslan II</a> (reigned 1156–1192.)</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ahi_Elvan_Mosque">Ahi Elvan Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Ahi Elvan Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It was founded in the Ulus quarter near the Ankara Citadel and was constructed by the <a href="/wiki/Ahis" title="Ahis">Ahi fraternity</a> during the late 14th and early 15th centuries. The finely carved walnut member (pulpic) is of particular interest.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hac.C4.B1_Bayram_Mosque">Hacı Bayram Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Hacı Bayram Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This mosque, in the Ulus quarter next to the <a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Temple of Augustus</a>, was built in the early 15th century in <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_architecture" title="Seljuk architecture">Seljuk style</a> by an unknown architect. It was subsequently restored by architect <a href="/wiki/Mimar_Sinan" title="Mimar Sinan">Mimar Sinan</a> in the 16th century, with <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya" title="Kütahya">Kütahya</a> tiles being added in the 18th century. The mosque was built in honor of <a href="/wiki/Hac%C4%B1_Bayram-%C4%B1_Veli" title="Hacı Bayram-ı Veli">Hacı Bayram-ı Veli</a>, whose tomb is next to the mosque, two years before his death (1427–28).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The usable space inside this mosque is 437&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (4,704&#160;sq&#160;ft) on the first floor and 263&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (2,831&#160;sq&#160;ft) on the second floor.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Yeni_.28Cenab_Ahmet.29_Mosque">Yeni (Cenab Ahmet) Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Yeni (Cenab Ahmet) Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It is the largest Ottoman mosque in Ankara and was built by the famous architect Sinan in the 16th century. The mimber (pulpit) and mihrap (prayer niche) are of white marble, and the mosque itself is of Ankara stone, an example of very fine workmanship. Yeni Cami is on Ulucanlar Avenue.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kocatepe_Mosque">Kocatepe Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Kocatepe Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kocatepe_Mosque" title="Kocatepe Mosque">Kocatepe Mosque</a> is the largest mosque in the city. Located in the Kocatepe quarter, it was constructed between 1967 and 1987 in classical <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman style</a> with four minarets. Its size and prominent location have made it a landmark for the city.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ahmet_Hamdi_Akseki_Mosque">Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque is located near the Presidency of Religious Affairs on the <a href="/wiki/Eskisehir" title="Eskisehir" class="mw-redirect">Eskisehir</a> road. Built in the neoclassical style this mosque is one of the largest new mosques in the city (construction finished in 2013). Its capacity is 6 thousand people in general and 30 thousand people for the funeral prayer. In decoration of the Mosque Anatolian Seljuk's patterns were used.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inns">Inns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Inns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suluhan">Suluhan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Suluhan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Suluhan,_Ankara,_Turkey.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/220px-Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/330px-Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/440px-Suluhan%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Suluhan,_Ankara,_Turkey.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Suluhan" title="Suluhan">Suluhan Inn</a> (1511)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Suluhan" title="Suluhan">Suluhan</a> is a historical Inn in Ankara. It is also called the <i>Hasanpaşa Han</i>. It is about 400 meters (1,300&#160;ft) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Ulus_Square" title="Ulus Square">Ulus Square</a> and situated in the Hacıdoğan neighbourhood. According to the <i>vakfiye</i> (inscription) of the building, the Ottoman era <i>han</i> was commissioned by Hasan Pasha, a regional <a href="/wiki/Beylerbey" title="Beylerbey">beylerbey</a>, and was constructed between 1508 and 1511, during the final years of the reign of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_II" title="Bayezid II">Bayezid II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ank_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ank-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".C3.87engelhan_Rahmi_Ko.C3.A7_Museum">Çengelhan Rahmi Koç Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Çengelhan Rahmi Koç Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/%C3%87engelhan_Rahmi_Ko%C3%A7_Museum" title="Çengelhan Rahmi Koç Museum" class="mw-redirect">Çengelhan Rahmi Koç Museum</a> is a museum of industrial technology situated in <a href="//tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87engel_Han" class="extiw" title="tr:Çengel Han">Çengel Han</a>, an Ottoman era Inn which was completed in 1523, during the early years of the reign of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>. The exhibits include industrial/technological artifacts from the 1850s onwards.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_monuments">Modern monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Modern monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Victory_Monument">Victory Monument</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Victory Monument">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg/220px-Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg/330px-Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg/440px-Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceremonial_standard003.Ankara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hattians" title="Hattians">Hatti</a> Monument (1970) on <a href="/wiki/S%C4%B1hhiye_Square" title="Sıhhiye Square">Sıhhiye Square</a>. It was the city's official logo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Victory_Monument_(Ankara)" title="Victory Monument (Ankara)">Victory Monument</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i><a href="//tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Zafer_An%C4%B1t%C4%B1" class="extiw" title="tr:Ankara Zafer Anıtı">Zafer Anıtı</a></i>) was crafted by Austrian sculptor Heinrich Krippel in 1925 and was erected in 1927 at <a href="/wiki/Ulus_Square" title="Ulus Square">Ulus Square</a>. The monument is made of <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> and features an <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue" title="Equestrian statue">equestrian statue</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>, who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" title="Field Marshal" class="mw-redirect">Field Marshal</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statue_of_Atat.C3.BCrk">Statue of Atatürk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Statue of Atatürk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Located at Zafer Square (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i>Zafer Meydanı</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> statue was crafted by the renowned Italian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Canonica" title="Pietro Canonica">Pietro Canonica</a> in 1927 and depicts a standing Atatürk who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" title="Field Marshal" class="mw-redirect">Field Marshal</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Monument_to_a_Secure.2C_Confident_Future">Monument to a Secure, Confident Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Monument to a Secure, Confident Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This monument, located in Güven Park near Kızılay Square, was erected in 1935 and bears Atatürk's advice to his people: "Turk! Be proud, work hard, and believe in yourself."</p>
<p>The monument was depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the Turkish 5 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknote of 1937–1952<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and of the 1000 lira banknotes of 1939–1946.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hatti_Monument">Hatti Monument</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Hatti Monument">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Built in the 1970s on <a href="/wiki/S%C4%B1hhiye_Square" title="Sıhhiye Square">Sıhhiye Square</a>, this impressive monument symbolizes the <a href="/wiki/Hattians" title="Hattians">Hatti</a> gods and commemorates Anatolia's earliest known civilization. The symbol derived from this monument has been used as the logo of the city for a long time.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Metro" title="Ankara Metro">Ankara Metro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Central_Station" title="Ankara Central Station" class="mw-redirect">Ankara Central Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esenbo%C4%9Fa_International_Airport" title="Esenboğa International Airport">Esenboğa International Airport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG/220px-%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG/330px-%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG/440px-%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%87ayyolu_Metro_19.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A subway train of the M2 line at the <a href="/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square" title="Kızılay Square" class="mw-redirect">Kızılay</a> station of the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Metro" title="Ankara Metro">Ankara Metro</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG/220px-Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG/330px-Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG/440px-Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Central_Station_2012_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/TCDD_HT65000" title="TCDD HT65000">TCDD HT65000</a> <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey" title="High-speed rail in Turkey">high-speed train</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Central_Station" title="Ankara Central Station" class="mw-redirect">Ankara Central Station</a> (1937)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Electricity, Gas, Bus General Directorate</i> (EGO)<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> operates the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Metro" title="Ankara Metro">Ankara Metro</a> and other forms of public transportation. Ankara is currently served by a <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">suburban rail</a> named <a href="/wiki/Ankaray" title="Ankaray" class="mw-redirect">Ankaray</a> (A1) and three <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subway</a> lines (M1, M2, M3) of the Ankara Metro with about 300,000 total daily commuters, while an additional subway line (M4) is currently under construction. A 3.2&#160;km (2.0&#160;mi) long <a href="/wiki/Gondola_lift" title="Gondola lift">gondola lift</a> with four stations connects the district of Şentepe to the <a href="/wiki/Yenimahalle,_Ankara" title="Yenimahalle, Ankara">Yenimahalle metro station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Central_Station" title="Ankara Central Station" class="mw-redirect">Ankara Central Station</a> is a major rail hub in Turkey. The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways" title="Turkish State Railways">Turkish State Railways</a> operates passenger train service from Ankara to other major cities, such as: <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul" title="İstanbul" class="mw-redirect">İstanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir" title="Eskişehir">Eskişehir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bal%C4%B1kesir" title="Balıkesir">Balıkesir</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya" title="Kütahya">Kütahya</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kayseri" title="Kayseri">Kayseri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adana" title="Adana">Adana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kars" title="Kars">Kars</a>, <a href="/wiki/El%C3%A2z%C4%B1%C4%9F" title="Elâzığ" class="mw-redirect">Elâzığ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malatya" title="Malatya">Malatya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diyarbak%C4%B1r" title="Diyarbakır">Diyarbakır</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karab%C3%BCk" title="Karabük">Karabük</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zonguldak" title="Zonguldak">Zonguldak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sivas" title="Sivas">Sivas</a>. Commuter rail also runs between the stations of <a href="/wiki/Sincan-Kaya%C5%9F_Line" title="Sincan-Kayaş Line">Sincan and Kayaş</a>. On 13 March 2009, the new <a href="/wiki/Y%C3%BCksek_H%C4%B1zl%C4%B1_Tren" title="Yüksek Hızlı Tren">Yüksek Hızlı Tren</a> (YHT) <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey" title="High-speed rail in Turkey">high-speed rail service</a> began operation between Ankara and Eskişehir. On 23 August 2011, another YHT high-speed line commercially started its service <a href="/wiki/Ankara-Konya_high-speed_railway" title="Ankara-Konya high-speed railway">between Ankara and Konya</a>. On 25 July 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Ankara-Istanbul_high-speed_railway" title="Ankara-Istanbul high-speed railway">Ankara–Istanbul high-speed line</a> of YHT entered service.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.asti.com.tr/">Ankara Intercity Bus Terminal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Ankara Şehirlerarası Terminal İşletmesi, AŞTİ</i></span>) is an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Bus_network" title="Bus network">bus network</a> which covers every neighbourhood in the city. Bus tickets from all other cities to Ankara can be found at Otobusbileti.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Esenbo%C4%9Fa_International_Airport" title="Esenboğa International Airport">Esenboğa International Airport</a>, located in the north-east of the city, is Ankara's main airport.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:958px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg" class="image" title="Esenboğa International Airport"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/950px-Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg" width="950" height="205" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/1425px-Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/1900px-Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2118" data-file-height="457" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Esenbo%C4%9Fa_International_Airport" title="Esenboğa International Airport">Esenboğa International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Arena.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ankara_Arena.JPG/220px-Ankara_Arena.JPG" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ankara_Arena.JPG/330px-Ankara_Arena.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ankara_Arena.JPG/440px-Ankara_Arena.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1566" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Arena.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ankara_Arena" title="Ankara Arena">Ankara Arena</a> (2010)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As with all other cities of Turkey, football is the most popular sport in Ankara. The city has one <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football club</a> currently competing in the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="Süper Lig">Turkish Super League</a>: <a href="/wiki/Gen%C3%A7lerbirli%C4%9Fi_S.K." title="Gençlerbirliği S.K.">Gençlerbirliği</a>, founded in 1923, is known as the <i>Ankara Gale</i> or the <i>Poppies</i> because of their colors: red and black. They were the Turkish Cup winners in 1987 and 2001. <a href="/wiki/Ankarag%C3%BCc%C3%BC" title="Ankaragücü" class="mw-redirect">Ankaragücü</a>, founded in 1910, is the oldest club in Ankara and is associated with Ankara's military arsenal manufacturing company MKE. Ankaragücü used to play in the Turkish Super League until being relegated to the <a href="/wiki/TFF_First_League" title="TFF First League">TFF First League</a> at the end of the 2011–2012 season. They were the <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_Kupas%C4%B1" title="Türkiye Kupası" class="mw-redirect">Turkish Cup</a> winners in 1972 and 1981. Gençlerbirliği's B team, <a href="/wiki/Hacettepe_Spor_Kul%C3%BCb%C3%BC" title="Hacettepe Spor Kulübü" class="mw-redirect">Hacettepe SK</a> (formerly known as Gençlerbirliği OFTAŞ) played in the Turkish Super League for a while until being relegated. All of the aforementioned teams have their home at the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_19_May%C4%B1s_Stadium" title="Ankara 19 Mayıs Stadium">Ankara 19 Mayıs Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ulus,_Ankara" title="Ulus, Ankara">Ulus</a>, which has a capacity of 21,250 (all-seater).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> A fourth team, <a href="/wiki/Ankaraspor_A.%C5%9E." title="Ankaraspor A.Ş." class="mw-redirect">Büyükşehir Belediye Ankaraspor</a>, played in the Turkish Super League until 2010, when they were expelled, and currently are not a member of the Turkish league system. Their home was the <a href="/wiki/Yenikent_Asa%C5%9F_Stadium" title="Yenikent Asaş Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Yenikent Asaş Stadium</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sincan,_Ankara" title="Sincan, Ankara">Sincan</a> district of Yenikent, outside the city center.</p>
<p>Ankara has a large number of minor teams, playing at regional levels: <a href="/wiki/ABB_Bugsa%C5%9F_S.K." title="ABB Bugsaş S.K." class="mw-redirect">Bugsaşspor</a> in Sincan; <a href="/wiki/Etimesgut_%C5%9Eekerspor" title="Etimesgut Şekerspor" class="mw-redirect">Etimesgut Şekerspor</a> in Etimesgut; <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekomspor" title="Türk Telekomspor" class="mw-redirect">Türk Telekomspor</a> owned by the phone company in Yenimahalle; <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Demirspor" title="Ankara Demirspor">Ankara Demirspor</a> in Çankaya; <a href="/wiki/Ke%C3%A7i%C3%B6reng%C3%BCc%C3%BC" title="Keçiörengücü">Keçiörengücü</a>, Keçiörenspor, <a href="/wiki/Pursaklarspor" title="Pursaklarspor" class="mw-redirect">Pursaklarspor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%9Flumspor" title="Bağlumspor">Bağlumspor</a> in Keçiören; and <a href="/wiki/Petrol_Ofisi_Spor" title="Petrol Ofisi Spor" class="mw-redirect">Petrol Ofisi Spor</a> owned by the oil company in Altındağ. Most of them, including <a href="/wiki/Hacettepespor" title="Hacettepespor" class="mw-redirect">Hacettepespor</a>, play their matches at <a href="/wiki/Cebeci_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC_Stadium" title="Cebeci İnönü Stadium">Cebeci İnönü Stadium</a> in the Cebeci district.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Basketball_League" title="Turkish Basketball League" class="mw-redirect">Turkish Basketball League</a>, Ankara is represented by <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom" title="Türk Telekom">Türk Telekom</a>, whose home is the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Arena" title="Ankara Arena">Ankara Arena</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TED_Kolejliler" title="TED Kolejliler" class="mw-redirect">CASA TED Kolejliler</a>, whose home is the TOBB Sports Hall.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Halkbank_Ankara" title="Halkbank Ankara">Halkbank Ankara</a> is currently the leading domestic powerhouse in Men's Volleyball, having won many championships and cups in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Men%27s_Volleyball_League" title="Turkish Men's Volleyball League">Turkish Men's Volleyball League</a> and even the <a href="/wiki/CEV_Cup" title="CEV Cup">CEV Cup</a> in 2013.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ankara_Ice_Palace" title="Ankara Ice Palace">Ankara Buz Pateni Sarayı</a> is where the <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">ice skating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> competitions take place in the city.</p>
<p>There are many popular spots for <a href="/wiki/Skateboarding" title="Skateboarding">skateboarding</a> which is active in the city since the 1980s. Skaters in Ankara usually meet in the park near the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey" title="Grand National Assembly of Turkey">Grand National Assembly of Turkey</a>.</p>
<p>The 2012-built <a href="/wiki/THF_Sport_Hall" title="THF Sport Hall">THF Sport Hall</a> hosts the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Handball_Super_League" title="Turkish Handball Super League">Handball Super League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Women%27s_Handball_Super_League" title="Turkish Women's Handball Super League">Women's Handball Super League</a> matches scheduled in Ankara.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_education">Culture and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Culture and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG/220px-TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG/330px-TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG/440px-TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TurkishStateTheatresHeadOfficeInAnkara.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The historic Evkaf Apartmanı (1929) is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Theatres" title="Turkish State Theatres">Turkish State Theatres</a>. The building also houses the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Tiyatro" title="Küçük Tiyatro">Küçük Tiyatro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oda_Tiyatrosu" title="Oda Tiyatrosu">Oda Tiyatrosu</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG/220px-AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG/330px-AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG/440px-AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1688" data-file-height="820" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AnkaraStateOpera2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House" title="Ankara Opera House">Ankara Opera House</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Opera_and_Ballet" title="Turkish State Opera and Ballet">Turkish State Opera and Ballet</a> (1933)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg/220px-Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg/330px-Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg/440px-Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2045" data-file-height="1314" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilkent_concert_hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bilkent_Concert_Hall" title="Bilkent Concert Hall">Bilkent Concert Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Opera_and_Ballet" title="Turkish State Opera and Ballet">Turkish State Opera and Ballet</a>, the national directorate of opera and ballet companies of Turkey, has its headquarters in Ankara, and serves the city with three venues:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House" title="Ankara Opera House">Ankara Opera House</a> (<i>Opera Sahnesi</i>, also known as <i>Büyük Tiyatro</i>) is the largest of the three venues for opera and ballet in Ankara.</li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Theatres" title="Turkish State Theatres">Turkish State Theatres</a> also has its head office in Ankara and runs the following stages in the city:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/125._Y%C4%B1l_%C3%87ayyolu_Sahnesi" title="125. Yıl Çayyolu Sahnesi">125. Yıl Çayyolu Sahnesi</a></li>
<li><a href="//tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Devlet_Tiyatrosu" class="extiw" title="tr:Ankara Devlet Tiyatrosu">Büyük Tiyatro</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Tiyatro" title="Küçük Tiyatro">Küçük Tiyatro</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C5%9Einasi_Sahnesi" title="Şinasi Sahnesi">Şinasi Sahnesi</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ak%C3%BCn_Sahnesi" title="Akün Sahnesi" class="mw-redirect">Akün Sahnesi</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alt%C4%B1nda%C4%9F_Tiyatrosu" title="Altındağ Tiyatrosu">Altındağ Tiyatrosu</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0rfan_%C5%9Eahinba%C5%9F_At%C3%B6lye_Sahnesi" title="İrfan Şahinbaş Atölye Sahnesi">İrfan Şahinbaş Atölye Sahnesi</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oda_Tiyatrosu" title="Oda Tiyatrosu">Oda Tiyatrosu</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mahir_Canova_Sahnesi" title="Mahir Canova Sahnesi">Mahir Canova Sahnesi</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Muhsin_Ertu%C4%9Frul_Sahnesi" title="Muhsin Ertuğrul Sahnesi">Muhsin Ertuğrul Sahnesi</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>In addition, the city is served by several private theatre companies, among which <a href="//tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Sanat_Tiyatrosu" class="extiw" title="tr:Ankara Sanat Tiyatrosu">Ankara Sanat Tiyatrosu</a>, who have their own stage in the city center, is a notable example.</p>
<p>Ankara is host to five classical music orchestras:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Presidential_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Presidential Symphony Orchestra">Presidential Symphony Orchestra</a> (Turkish Presidential Symphony Orchestra)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bilkent_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Bilkent Symphony Orchestra">Bilkent Symphony Orchestra</a> (BSO) is a major symphony orchestra of Turkey.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hacettepe_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Hacettepe Symphony Orchestra">Hacettepe Symphony Orchestra</a> was founded in 2003 and is currently conducted by Erol Erdinç.</li>
<li><b>Başkent Oda Orkestrası</b> (Chamber Orchestra of the Capital)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>There are four concert halls in the city:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/CSO_Concert_Hall" title="CSO Concert Hall">CSO Concert Hall</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bilkent_Concert_Hall" title="Bilkent Concert Hall">Bilkent Concert Hall</a> is a performing arts center in Ankara. It is located in the Bilkent University campus.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MEB_%C5%9Eura_Salonu" title="MEB Şura Salonu">MEB Şura Salonu</a> (also known as the Festival Hall), It is noted for its tango performances.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya_%C3%87a%C4%9Fda%C5%9F_Sanatlar_Merkezi_Concert_Hall" title="Çankaya Çağdaş Sanatlar Merkezi Concert Hall">Çankaya Çağdaş Sanatlar Merkezi Concert Hall</a> was founded in 1994.</li>
</ul>
<p>The city has been host to several well-established, annual theatre, music, film festivals:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="//tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Uluslararas%C4%B1_M%C3%BCzik_Festivali" class="extiw" title="tr:Ankara Uluslararası Müzik Festivali">Ankara International Music Festival</a>, a music festival organized in the Turkish capital presenting classical music and ballet programmes.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ankara also has a number of concert venues such as <i><a href="/wiki/IF_Performance_Hall" title="IF Performance Hall">IF Performance Hall</a></i>, <i>Eskiyeni</i>, <i>Jolly Joker</i>, <i>Kite</i>, <i>Nefes Bar</i>, <i>Noxus Pub</i> and <i>Passage Pub</i>, which host the live performances and events of popular musicians.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_cat">Angora cat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Angora cat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Turkish Angora</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/170px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/255px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/340px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Angora_cat" title="Angora cat" class="mw-redirect">Angora cat</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ankara is home to a world famous domestic <a href="/wiki/Cat_breed" title="Cat breed" class="mw-redirect">cat breed</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Turkish Angora</a>, called <i>Ankara kedisi</i> (Ankara cat) in Turkish. Turkish Angoras are one of the ancient, naturally occurring cat breeds, having originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.</p>
<p>They mostly have a white, silky, medium to long length coat, no undercoat and a fine bone structure. There seems to be a connection between the Angora Cats and <a href="/wiki/Persian_(cat)" title="Persian (cat)" class="mw-redirect">Persians</a>, and the Turkish Angora is also a distant cousin of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Van" title="Turkish Van">Turkish Van</a>. Although they are known for their shimmery white coat, currently there are more than twenty varieties including black, blue and reddish fur. They come in <a href="/wiki/Tabby_cat" title="Tabby cat">tabby</a> and tabby-white, along with smoke varieties, and are in every color other than pointed, lavender, and cinnamon (all of which would indicate breeding to an outcross.)</p>
<p>Eyes may be blue, green, or amber, or even one blue and one amber or green. The W gene which is responsible for the white coat and blue eye is closely related to the hearing ability, and the presence of a blue eye can indicate that the cat is deaf to the side the blue eye is located. However, a great many blue and <a href="/wiki/Odd-eyed_cat" title="Odd-eyed cat">odd-eyed</a> white cats have normal hearing, and even deaf cats lead a very normal life if kept indoors.</p>
<p>Ears are pointed and large, eyes are almond shaped and the head is massive with a two plane profile. Another characteristic is the tail, which is often kept parallel to the back.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_rabbit">Angora rabbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Angora rabbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/170px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/255px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/340px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Ankara tavşanı</i></span>) is a variety of domestic rabbit bred for its long, soft hair. The Angora is one of the oldest types of domestic rabbit, originating in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia, along with the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Angora cat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a>. The rabbits were popular pets with French royalty in the mid-18th century, and spread to other parts of Europe by the end of the century. They first appeared in the United States in the early 20th century. They are bred largely for their long <a href="/wiki/Angora_wool" title="Angora wool">Angora wool</a>, which may be removed by <a href="/wiki/Sheep_shearing" title="Sheep shearing">shearing</a>, combing, or <a href="/wiki/Plucking_(hair_removal)" title="Plucking (hair removal)">plucking</a> (gently pulling loose wool.)</p>
<p>Angoras are bred mainly for their wool because it is silky and soft. They have a humorous appearance, as they oddly resemble a fur ball. Most are calm and docile but should be handled carefully. Grooming is necessary to prevent the fiber from matting and felting on the rabbit. A condition called "wool block" is common in Angora rabbits and should be treated quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Sometimes they are shorn in the summer as the long fur can cause the rabbits to overheat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_goat">Angora goat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Angora goat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quebec_angora_goat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/170px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/255px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/340px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quebec_angora_goat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Ankara keçisi</i></span>) is a breed of <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">domestic goat</a> that originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.</p>
<p>This breed was first mentioned in the time of <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>, roughly in 1500&#160;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The first Angora goats were brought to Europe by <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, about 1554, but, like later imports, were not very successful. Angora goats were first introduced in the United States in 1849 by Dr. James P. Davis. Seven adult goats were a gift from Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I" title="Abdülmecid I">Abdülmecid I</a> in appreciation for his services and advice on the raising of cotton.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pile_(textile)" title="Pile (textile)">fleece</a> taken from an Angora goat is called <a href="/wiki/Mohair" title="Mohair">mohair</a>. A single goat produces between five and eight kilograms of hair per year. Angoras are shorn twice a year, unlike <a href="/wiki/Domestic_sheep" title="Domestic sheep" class="mw-redirect">sheep</a>, which are shorn only once. Angoras have high nutritional requirements due to their rapid hair growth. A poor quality diet will curtail mohair development. The United States, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, and South Africa are the top producers of mohair.</p>
<p>For a long period of time, Angora goats were bred for their white coat. In 1998, the Colored Angora Goat Breeders Association was set up to promote breeding of colored Angoras. Today, Angora goats produce white, black (deep black to greys and silver), red (the color fades significantly as the goat gets older), and brownish fiber.</p>
<p>Angora goats were depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the Turkish 50 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknotes of 1938–1952.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The citadel was depicted in the following Turkish banknotes:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">obverse</a> of the 1 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknote of 1927–1939 (1. Emission Group – One Turkish Lira – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/6.htm">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the obverse of the 5 lira banknote of 1927–1937 (1. Emission Group – Five Turkish Lira – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/10.htm">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the 10 lira banknote of 1927–1938 (1. Emission Group – Ten Turkish Lira – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/14.htm">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the reverse of the 10 lira banknote of 1938–1952 (2. Emission Group – Ten Turkish Lira – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E2/52.htm">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the reverse of the 100 lira banknotes of 1983–1989 (7. Emission Group – One Hundred Turkish Lira – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E7/256.htm">I.
